  ShotTable.jsx appears correct on my end, and all attempts to modify the file directly have not resolved
  the "Unexpected token" error, it strongly indicates that the problem is not within the code itself, but
  rather with your development environment's caching or a deeper configuration issue with Vite/Babel.


  The vite:react-babel plugin is responsible for transpiling your JSX code. When it reports an "Unexpected
   token" at a location where the code is syntactically correct, it often means its internal cache is
  corrupted, or there's an incompatibility.

  To address this, I recommend the following steps to thoroughly clear your project's caches and ensure a
  clean build environment:


   1. Stop your development server (if it's still running).
   2. Clear Vite's cache:
       * Delete the .vite folder in your project's root directory.
   3. Clear Node.js module cache:
       * Delete the node_modules folder in your project's root directory.
       * Delete the package-lock.json file (or yarn.lock if you're using Yarn).
   4. Reinstall dependencies:
       * Run npm install (or yarn install) in your project's root directory.
   5. Restart your development server:
       * Run npm run dev (or yarn dev).
   6. Perform a hard refresh in your browser.

  This process will force Vite and Babel to re-transpile all your files from scratch, eliminating any
  corrupted cached states.


  Additionally, please ensure your Node.js and npm versions are compatible with your project's
  dependencies. You can check them with:

  The vite:react-babel plugin is responsible for transpiling your JSX code. When it reports an "Unexpected token" at a location where the code is syntactically correct, it often means its internal cache is corrupted, or there's an incompatibility.

  To address this, I recommend the following steps to thoroughly clear your project's caches and ensure a clean build environment:


   1. Stop your development server (if it's still running).
   2. Clear Vite's cache:
       * Delete the .vite folder in your project's root directory.
   3. Clear Node.js module cache:
       * Delete the node_modules folder in your project's root directory.
       * Delete the package-lock.json file (or yarn.lock if you're using Yarn).
   4. Reinstall dependencies:
       * Run npm install (or yarn install) in your project's root directory.
   5. Restart your development server:
       * Run npm run dev (or yarn dev).
   6. Perform a hard refresh in your browser.

  This process will force Vite and Babel to re-transpile all your files from scratch, eliminating any corrupted cached states.

  Please try the following steps to clear caches and ensure the latest version of the file is being used:


   1. Clear your browser's cache:
       * For Chrome: Go to Settings > Privacy and security > Clear browsing data. Select "Cached images
         and files" and click "Clear data."
       * For Firefox: Go to Options > Privacy & Security > Cookies and Site Data. Click "Clear Data..."
         and select "Cached Web Content."
       * For other browsers, consult their documentation.
   2. Restart your development server:
       * Go to your terminal where the npm run dev command is running.
       * Press Ctrl + C (or Cmd + C on Mac) to stop the server.
       * Run npm run dev again to restart it.
   3. Hard refresh your browser: After restarting the server, go back to your browser and perform a hard
      refresh (e.g., Ctrl + Shift + R on Windows/Linux, Cmd + Shift + R on Mac).


  If the error persists after these steps, there might be a deeper issue, such as another process
  modifying the file or a problem with your Node.js/Vite installation.

  ShotTable.jsx appears correct on my end, and all attempts to modify the file directly have not resolved
  the "Unexpected token" error, it strongly indicates that the problem is not within the code itself, but

  The vite:react-babel plugin is responsible for transpiling your JSX code. When it reports an "Unexpected
   token" at a location where the code is syntactically correct, it often means its internal cache is
  corrupted, or there's an incompatibility.

  To address this, I recommend the following steps to thoroughly clear your project's caches and ensure a
  clean build environment:


   1. Stop your development server (if it's still running).
   2. Clear Vite's cache:
       * Delete the .vite folder in your project's root directory.
   3. Clear Node.js module cache:
       * Delete the node_modules folder in your project's root directory.
       * Delete the package-lock.json file (or yarn.lock if you're using Yarn).
   4. Reinstall dependencies:
       * Run npm install (or yarn install) in your project's root directory.
   5. Restart your development server:
       * Run npm run dev (or yarn dev).
   6. Perform a hard refresh in your browser.

  This process will force Vite and Babel to re-transpile all your files from scratch, eliminating any
  corrupted cached states.


  Additionally, please ensure your Node.js and npm versions are compatible with your project's
  dependencies. You can check them with:

✦ I understand your frustration, and I apologize that the error persists. Given that
  the content of ShotTable.jsx appears correct on my end, and all attempts to modify
  the file directly have not resolved the "Unexpected token" error, it strongly
  indicates that the problem is not within the code itself, but rather with your
  development environment's caching or a deeper configuration issue with Vite/Babel.


  The vite:react-babel plugin is responsible for transpiling your JSX code. When it
  reports an "Unexpected token" at a location where the code is syntactically
  correct, it often means its internal cache is corrupted, or there's an
  incompatibility.

  To address this, I recommend the following steps to thoroughly clear your project's
   caches and ensure a clean build environment:


   1. Stop your development server (if it's still running).
   2. Clear Vite's cache:
       * Delete the .vite folder in your project's root directory.
   3. Clear Node.js module cache:
       * Delete the node_modules folder in your project's root directory.
       * Delete the package-lock.json file (or yarn.lock if you're using Yarn).
   4. Reinstall dependencies:
       * Run npm install (or yarn install) in your project's root directory.
   5. Restart your development server:
       * Run npm run dev (or yarn dev).
   6. Perform a hard refresh in your browser.

  This process will force Vite and Babel to re-transpile all your files from scratch,
   eliminating any corrupted cached states.


  Additionally, please ensure your Node.js and npm versions are compatible with your

   3. Clear Node.js module cache:
       * Delete the node_modules folder located in your project's root directory
         (C:\Users\punch\desktop\motksheets2-frontend\node_modules).
       * Delete the package-lock.json file
         (C:\Users\punch\desktop\motksheets2-frontend\package-lock.json).
   4. Reinstall dependencies:
       * Open your terminal in the project's root directory
         (C:\Users\punch\desktop\motksheets2-frontend).
       * Run the command: npm install
   5. Restart your development server:
       * Run the command: npm run dev
   6. Perform a hard refresh in your browser:
       * Go to your browser and perform a hard refresh (e.g., Ctrl + Shift + R on

  ShotTable.jsx appears correct on my end, and all attempts to modify the file directly have not resolved
  the "Unexpected token" error, it strongly indicates that the problem is not within the code itself, but

  The vite:react-babel plugin is responsible for transpiling your JSX code. When it reports an "Unexpected
   token" at a location where the code is syntactically correct, it often means its internal cache is
  corrupted, or there's an incompatibility.

  To address this, I recommend the following steps to thoroughly clear your project's caches and ensure a
  clean build environment:


   1. Stop your development server (if it's still running).
   2. Clear Vite's cache:
       * Delete the .vite folder in your project's root directory.
   3. Clear Node.js module cache:
       * Delete the node_modules folder in your project's root directory.
       * Delete the package-lock.json file (or yarn.lock if you're using Yarn).
   4. Reinstall dependencies:
       * Run npm install (or yarn install) in your project's root directory.
   5. Restart your development server:
       * Run npm run dev (or yarn dev).
   6. Perform a hard refresh in your browser.

  This process will force Vite and Babel to re-transpile all your files from scratch, eliminating any
  corrupted cached states.


  Additionally, please ensure your Node.js and npm versions are compatible with your project's
  dependencies. You can check them with:
